  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3e370581-2d53-4366-9d68-d0ec68a07b78'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12571289360981682105">Great Britain circa 1985: time travel is routine, cloning is a reality (dodos are the resurrected pet of choice), and literature is taken very, very seriously. Baconians are trying to convince the world that Francis Bacon really wrote Shakespeare, there are riots between the Surrealists and Impressionists, and thousands of men are named John Milton, an homage to the real M</span>
  <span id="freeText12571289360981682105" style="display:none">Great Britain circa 1985: time travel is routine, cloning is a reality (dodos are the resurrected pet of choice), and literature is taken very, very seriously. Baconians are trying to convince the world that Francis Bacon really wrote Shakespeare, there are riots between the Surrealists and Impressionists, and thousands of men are named John Milton, an homage to the real Milton and a very confusing situation for the police. Amidst all this, Acheron Hades, Third Most Wanted Man In the World, steals the original manuscript of Martin Chuzzlewit and kills a minor character, who then disappears from every volume of the novel ever printed! But that's just a prelude . . .<br /><br />Hades' real target is the beloved Jane Eyre, and it's not long before he plucks her from the pages of Bronte's novel. Enter Thursday Next. She's the Special Operative's renowned literary detective, and she drives a Porsche. With the help of her uncle Mycroft's Prose Portal, Thursday enters the novel to rescue Jane Eyre from this heinous act of literary homicide. It's tricky business, all these interlopers running about Thornfield, and deceptions run rampant as their paths cross with Jane, Rochester, and Miss Fairfax. Can Thursday save Jane Eyre and Bronte's masterpiece? And what of the Crimean War? Will it ever end? And what about those annoying black holes that pop up now and again, sucking things into time-space voids . . .<br /><br />Suspenseful and outlandish, absorbing and fun, The Eyre Affair is a caper unlike any other and an introduction to the imagination of a most distinctive writer and his singular fictional universe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12571289360981682105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1357564-does-anyone-know-why-there-is-no-chapter">Does anyone know why there is no Chapter 13 in The Eyre Affair? It&#39;s listed in the table of contents, but we immediately go from chapter 12 to chapter 14.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1357564'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F27003.The_Eyre_Affair">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1357564-does-anyone-know-why-there-is-no-chapter">2 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1357564-does-anyone-know-why-there-is-no-chapter">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/97039-emma"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1502092437i/97039._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/97039-emma">Emma</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">None of the author's books have a chapter 13.<br/><br/>On his website JF says the following on chapter 13 of book 1: "The Church at Capel-y-ffin; Capel-y-ffin i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">None of the author's books have a chapter 13.<br /><br />On his website JF says the following on chapter 13 of book 1: "The Church at Capel-y-ffin; Capel-y-ffin is a place in the Black Mountains in South Wales, not far from Hay-on-Wye; the name means 'the boundary chapel', (it is very close to Offa's Dyke, the ancient Anglo-Welsh boundary) and there is indeed a (very small) church there, as well as a youth hostel. My thanks to Ben for this information. Oh, you want to know why it's in the list of chapters? Well, I don't know for sure, but I suspect the word 'boojumed' to be relevant here."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

<div id="review_770906966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/770906966" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/770906966?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780143145707" href="/book/show/7031306-the-eyre-affair">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-would-blurb">books-i-would-blurb</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer770906966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12716133565019351157">I read this years ago, I think it was back around 2005 or so. <br/><br/>I remember liking the book fairly well, even though I'd never read Jane Eyre, and a modest part of the book's plot touches on that story. <br/><br/>But I also remember being irritated at the book. Something made me bristle when I read it. Some elements of the storytelling rubbed me the wrong way. <br/><br/>I remember talking to the person who recommended the book to me. I held it book up and said, rather disdainfully. "This is probably really popular, is</span>
  <span id="freeText12716133565019351157" style="display:none">I read this years ago, I think it was back around 2005 or so. <br /><br />I remember liking the book fairly well, even though I'd never read Jane Eyre, and a modest part of the book's plot touches on that story. <br /><br />But I also remember being irritated at the book. Something made me bristle when I read it. Some elements of the storytelling rubbed me the wrong way. <br /><br />I remember talking to the person who recommended the book to me. I held it book up and said, rather disdainfully. "This is probably really popular, isn't it?" <br /><br />My friend, who worked in a bookstore, said that no, actually, it wasn't all that popular. <br /><br />And as soon as she said that, I liked the book more. <br /><br />Thinking back, this memory disturbs me. And not only because it revealed a disturbing tendency towards the bullshit hipster I-only-like-things-nobody-else-likes mindset. <br /><br />Worse than that, I think it shows that I was getting a bit twisted up inside because of my inability to get my book published. <br /><br />You see, by the time 2005 rolled around, I'd been working on The Name of the Wind for about 11 years. 3 of those years I'd had an agent, and had been really *really* trying to get published. And it wasn't going so well. <br /><br />Well... actually that's not true. It was going well because I was on the road to being the published author I am today. But I didn't know that in 2005. Back then, all I knew is that I wasn't published *yet* and because of that, I was getting a little bitter. <br /><br />Well... to be fair, I was probably more than a little bitter. I was twisted up enough inside that even the perceived success of a book was enough to make it unpalatable to me. <br /><br />Which is a real shame, because jump forward to now, and I've been listening to the series as an audiobook and enjoying it immensely. <br /><br />It's well written and quickly paced. There's both humor and wit in ample supply. And the world is a delightfully tounge-in-cheek wish fulfillment alternate earth where the entire populace is passionately engaged in literature. There are museums dedicated to authors, political parties court the Chaucer block of voters, and Baconians go door to door, trying to convert people to their philosophy: namely, that Fredrick Bacon is the man who *actually* penned the plays credited to Shakespeare. <br /><br />Short version: If you're a recovering English major, or if you're just well read, odds are you're going to enjoy this book. Ditto if you're a writer... provided you're not the sort of twisted up bitter type of writer I was back in 2005. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12716133565019351157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6762140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6762140" />
    <a title="Jojo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/118531-jojo"><img alt="Jojo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544403747p2/118531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6762140?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jojo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jojo" href="/user/show/118531-jojo">Jojo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6762140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5987452350945271151">I had the same feeling after reading this as I had after reading <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i>. Fabulous idea, terrible execution. I was going to give it one more star than I gave that because it's not quite as badly written. And I liked the idea of door-to-door Baconians and <i>Rocky Horror</i>ized <i>Richard III</i>. But I changed my mind because the more I think about it, the more I didn't like it.<br/><br/>It was so smug and cutesy and in need of better editing. And it would have been better served by not being written in</span>
  <span id="freeText5987452350945271151" style="display:none">I had the same feeling after reading this as I had after reading <i>The Looking Glass Wars</i>. Fabulous idea, terrible execution. I was going to give it one more star than I gave that because it's not quite as badly written. And I liked the idea of door-to-door Baconians and <i>Rocky Horror</i>ized <i>Richard III</i>. But I changed my mind because the more I think about it, the more I didn't like it.<br /><br />It was so smug and cutesy and in need of better editing. And it would have been better served by not being written in first person, especially since it kept slipping into other people's heads when it should have been in Thursday's. Also, Thursday is really boring and doesn't have an interesting voice, and I didn't care about her at all (and, ick, that moment where she gets out her mirror and contemplates her looks). The same goes for most of the other characters. The only one I really liked was Thursday's father, and he barely had anything to do with anything. And the villain! How utterly boring. Villains are only interesting if they're something beyond mwahahaa so evil.<br /><br />And it was just a mess. So much random crap was going on that seemed to have nothing to do with anything. And I could have lived without the "romance" which was just yawningly boring and tacked on. And the names. Ugh. I wanted to stab my brain out having to read some of those awful names. <br /><br />Most people seem to adore this book and the rest of the series, but I thought it was pretty terrible. Maybe the writing gets better in later books, but I don't think I'll give them a chance.<br /><br />Very disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5987452350945271151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2319544507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319544507" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319544507?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=fforde-jasper">fforde-jasper</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319544507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5719591863827643915">Hardly an author has styled the parallel universe tropes with breaking the wall elements to such perfection as Ffjorde did.<br/><br/>The integration of living literature in a parallel universe as a plot device is ingenious and a potentially endless source of innuendos, connotations, and options for more and similar novels. Imagine the same with video games, movies, or all mixed and it could get big quick, depending on the main inspiration and idea of the chosen genres and works. <br/><br/>I´ve rarely ever chosen su</span>
  <span id="freeText5719591863827643915" style="display:none">Hardly an author has styled the parallel universe tropes with breaking the wall elements to such perfection as Ffjorde did.<br /><br />The integration of living literature in a parallel universe as a plot device is ingenious and a potentially endless source of innuendos, connotations, and options for more and similar novels. Imagine the same with video games, movies, or all mixed and it could get big quick, depending on the main inspiration and idea of the chosen genres and works. <br /><br />I´ve rarely ever chosen such a comparison, but I would name similarities to Adams, Pratchett, Robbins, and some others because of the humor, character development, and uniqueness. It´s really tricky to get an emotion out of me, but this amazing series did it several times.<br /><br />It´s an unconventional piece of literature, a true crossover hybrid that dances at many weddings, integrates, steals, persiflages, and makes me wonder why its quality is controversial. I see very much cherrypicking regarding the often average character and plot development of comedy and fast told stories that are necessary and essential for telling such a piece of literature. It smells for me like an aversion against too progressive, unconventional writing style, because I could hardly name a series that had both such a great idea, realization, and universal acclaimed greatness by everyone I recommended it too. <br /><br />If we start bashing each author who dares to explore completely new land of storytelling without getting artistic, boring, Nobel pricy, and bad, but instead keeps using the rules of the telling game in a brilliant new setting, many ideas will get lost. It shocked me to hear how long it took Ffjorde to get published and I think that many of the reasons for it lie in this grievance, in the tendency to troll true creativity because it´s too unfamiliar and strange to read.<br /><br />To make it clear: I don´t mean people who just can´t get warm with his writing style, what is a question of taste and personal preferences and completely ok, I am avoiding many genres too.<br /><br />I am more referring to people who rate very good, but stereotypical and always the same telling as usual high and are against progressive endeavours. Or the extreme other side, who love and read much high brow, so-called literature, that is often trash in my eyes, but bash popular fiction because of its predictability, popularity, and stereotypes or, if this is not the case as in this case, because it´s different. Nothing to talk about in academic circles, but something out of the line they can´t and don´t want to understand. <br /><br />Both groups are enemies of too progressive authors and it´s quite a shame that they, instead of staying in their own territory and not poaching in foreign lands, try out new things and don´t realize that their problems with the writing could be related to them and their subjective conditioning and thereby aversion and not a fault of an author. It´s so clear if someone interested in character-based, 3 setting novels reads Hard-Sci Fi space operas and vice versa, she/he won´t be happy with it and don´t like it because it´s not their thing, but in this case, the own reading preferences seem to have been forgotten. It´s like listening to music one hates and saying that the artist is bad, etc.<br /><br />This first part of this series has the only problem of info-dumping and explaining the world a bit too much instead of directly jumping into action, but that´s a widespread issue.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JasperFforde">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/ThursdayNext">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5719591863827643915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2369356628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2369356628" />
    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2369356628?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2369356628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1369477175681937202">Really enjoyed the inventiveness of Jasper Fforde's The Eyre Affair. The premise of the story is that original manuscripts can be stolen and then changed, not just that manuscript, but all copies of say, Jane Eyre. Thus, these original manuscripts are viewed as absolute treasures. There are also literary portals which intersect with the 'real world' which make it possible to change what happens in our favorite novel. And there's also time travel. And an alternate history which skews how we view </span>
  <span id="freeText1369477175681937202" style="display:none">Really enjoyed the inventiveness of Jasper Fforde's The Eyre Affair. The premise of the story is that original manuscripts can be stolen and then changed, not just that manuscript, but all copies of say, Jane Eyre. Thus, these original manuscripts are viewed as absolute treasures. There are also literary portals which intersect with the 'real world' which make it possible to change what happens in our favorite novel. And there's also time travel. And an alternate history which skews how we view this reality about 80 or 90 degrees. In Fforde's novel, our heroine, Thursday Next, tracks down a master criminal, a manuscript and interacts with the characters of Jane Eyre. However, the story unabashedly takes a backseat to literary puns and allusions and simple craziness. The world Fforde has created, a world both obsessed by books and with direct access to books, is a world book lovers will want to live in!<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534367543i/26135621._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sitting down with Jasper Fforde for fried rice, eggrolls and great discussion during a break at the Casper Humanities Festival!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1369477175681937202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_258108874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258108874" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7365405-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522094190p2/7365405.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258108874?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/7365405-james">James</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258108874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8137916895847358567">This book may describe my perfect job goal: to be able to enter a book and meet the characters, ensuring they are following the author's original intentions and not "on-the-loose" due to some sort of villain. How amazing would that be? Awesome kick start to this series... I read the first 4 then started to get a little disenchanted, but I'll go back one day! All book lovers need to give this first one a chance -- you'll undoubtedly love and hate parts of it!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_16792193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16792193" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/784513-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1220889844p2/784513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16792193?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/784513-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/784513-danielle?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16792193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13192867904583187388">I've been storing up some venom for this review, so be prepared.<br/>First of all, I want to unleash my fury on whoever in the Rory Gilmore Book Club suggested this book as February's pick. To go from such a brilliant read as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre' title='Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë' rel='nofollow noopener'> Jane Eyre</a> to this was frustrating to say the least. It highlighted all the amateurish contrivances of Fforde's writing. I rolled my eyes so many times in the first four chapters, that I nearly gave myself a headache. And no, I'm sure it doesn't get better after that, that's jus</span>
  <span id="freeText13192867904583187388" style="display:none">I've been storing up some venom for this review, so be prepared.<br />First of all, I want to unleash my fury on whoever in the Rory Gilmore Book Club suggested this book as February's pick. To go from such a brilliant read as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre" title="Jane Eyre by Charlotte Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jane Eyre</a> to this was frustrating to say the least. It highlighted all the amateurish contrivances of Fforde's writing. I rolled my eyes so many times in the first four chapters, that I nearly gave myself a headache. And no, I'm sure it doesn't get better after that, that's just where I officially banished the book from my sight.<br />Here are my major problems with the part I read.<br />1. Okay, you're enterting this alternate reality world where many things are similar but different from what we know. As Fforde might assume that not all of his readers would be British, or familiar with UK current events/history, perhaps he could have given us a little more to go on, so that the reader could appreciate the weirdness of this other world, without going, "Umm...from the way that's said, I'm assuming that's not how it happened in real life."<br />2. Thursday Next. Seriously? Thursday Next. That just screams: "I'm writing a strong yet lovably flawed female gumshoe destined to drag you through book after book of literary-themed exploits." Her character was so stereotypical I could have written it with my eyes closed.<br />3. The time-travelling father.<br />4. If a book is written in first-person, and you really, REALLY want us to know what the character looks like, it is textbook cliche to have her pull out a mirror and describe what she sees. Puh-lease.<br />5. Finally, the clincher at the end of chapter four (I think. I wasn't paying all THAT much attention), but the straw that made me put away the book for good is that Fforde CLEVERLY (I felt like the whole of the book was trying just a little too hard to be clever) had Thursday narrate what had happened in her confrontation with her nemesis by putting her in an interrogation setting, where she has to tell the police investigators (and us, conveniently) what happened prior to her month-long coma. Okay, that in and of itself is not so bad, what kills me is when the only difference between what she says into the tape recorder and what she says in her narration of any other part of the book is the double quotation marks. Seriously, no one answers an investigator's question of, "So what happened next," by saying, "'What do you think you're doing?' I said. 'It's time for me to make my exit,' he answered with a smile." People write books like that. They don't talk like that. It was ridiculous. <br />Anyway, I guess I wouldn't be so annoyed with this book, except that it's supposed to be "delightful" for bibliophiles because it assumes all this familiarity with the classics, yet anyone who had read said classics would inevitably chafe under the obvious inferiority of this freshman attempt.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13192867904583187388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166806315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166806315" />
    <a title="Cassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2282938-cassy"><img alt="Cassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565892954p2/2282938.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166806315?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassy" href="/user/show/2282938-cassy">Cassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9781435282032" href="/book/show/3435861-the-eyre-affair">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cassy by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=fiction-dsytopian-post-apocalyptic">fiction-dsytopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=region-europe">region-europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=region-elsewhere">region-elsewhere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=event-met-author">event-met-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=physical-own">physical-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=flavor-humor">flavor-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2282938-cassy?shelf=flavor-books-and-writing">flavor-books-and-writing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166806315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10514464350642408374">Have I become a jaded reader? I sometimes catch myself muttering in the middle of a long series of yawns, “Haven’t I read this plot/character/technique before?” Or when the author describes their setting, I will lazily flip through my mental inventory of backdrops until, sure enough, I find an old one that it is a good enough fit to reuse. <br/><br/>Then Fforde comes along and throws the literary equivalent of a bucket of Arctic cold water in my face. <br/><br/>I found myself having to actually work to keep up with</span>
  <span id="freeText10514464350642408374" style="display:none">Have I become a jaded reader? I sometimes catch myself muttering in the middle of a long series of yawns, “Haven’t I read this plot/character/technique before?” Or when the author describes their setting, I will lazily flip through my mental inventory of backdrops until, sure enough, I find an old one that it is a good enough fit to reuse. <br /><br />Then Fforde comes along and throws the literary equivalent of a bucket of Arctic cold water in my face. <br /><br />I found myself having to actually work to keep up with his creativity and humor. It was one of those amazing reciprocal relationships where the other party’s enthusiasm spurs you to try harder, which encourages them to go further, which forces you to run faster. <br /><br />At the same time, I was struck by how nonchalantly he presented the large and potentially confusing differences between our world and his. I also appreciated the attention he gave to the nitty-gritty level of his world. There were details so small that if you blinked, you’d miss them. As a result, I found myself reading each sentence carefully, word for word, and taking the time to create mental images from scratch. <br /><br />Here are some rough examples of what I’ve come to expect when I read a ho-hum book contrasted with the twists, both small and large, that Fforde introduced. <br /><br /><b>Example 1</b><br /><u>Expected</u>: Her name was Theresa Newton.<br /><u>Received</u>: Her name was Thursday Next.<br /><br /><b>Example 2</b><br /><u>Expected</u>: Theresa took her dog for a walk.<br /><u>Received</u>: Thursday took her dodo for a walk.<br /><br /><b>Example 3</b><br /><u>Expected</u>: Theresa boarded the plane for a trip home. <br /><u>Received</u>: Thursday boarded the airship for a trip home.<br /><br /><b>Example 4</b><br /><u>Expected</u>: Theresa opened the book and sat down for a nice, afternoon read. <br /><u>Received</u>: Thursday opened her book and fell into its alternate reality for a few months. <br /><br /><b>Example 5</b><br /><u>Expected</u>: Theresa’s dad stopped by the cafe and complained about her mom’s indecision about which color to paint their bedroom.<br /><u>Received</u>: Thursday’s dad stopped time to appear out of nowhere in the middle of the café and complained about the new shade of red her mother would paint their bedroom in two weeks time, which he saw when he visited the future.<br /><br />You get the point. <br /><br />I guess it all goes back to something I mentioned earlier: the reciprocal relationship. There are so many different layers to Fforde’s world-building. And he allows his readers to engage as deeply or superficially as they prefer. If you want to dive in, Fforde has those hidden nuggets for you to enjoy. Or if you want to invest your time just understanding the big points and push past the nuances, you’ll still come away satisfied. <br /><br />I’d personally recommend the all-in approach. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10514464350642408374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1204347107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204347107" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6564856-the-eyre-affair">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204347107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4724788709523406184"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jessica</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robin</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6950818.Kristi_Charish' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristi</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asya</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31718503-tanya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tanya</a>.</b> I apologize if I missed somebody; in case I did please let me know and I will add you. <br/><br/>The book version of mid-eighties England is a fine dystopian society. The literature is a very serious business, time travel is nothing of the ordinary which comes with all the fun and paradoxes and cloning works wonders making people's favorite pets out of these guys:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424971156i/13825326.gif' width='100' height='100' alt='dodo' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The heroine Thursday Next is a special operative working for literary detecti</span>
  <span id="freeText4724788709523406184" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6950818.Kristi_Charish" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristi</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya" rel="nofollow noopener">Asya</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31718503-tanya" rel="nofollow noopener">Tanya</a>.</b> I apologize if I missed somebody; in case I did please let me know and I will add you. <br><br>The book version of mid-eighties England is a fine dystopian society. The literature is a very serious business, time travel is nothing of the ordinary which comes with all the fun and paradoxes and cloning works wonders making people's favorite pets out of these guys:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424971156i/13825326.gif" width="100" height="100" alt="dodo" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The heroine Thursday Next is a special operative working for literary detection dealing with such heinous crimes as forging of a poem of a classic, theft of highly valued original manuscripts, and copyright violations. <br><br>What started as fairly unremarkable theft of an original Dickens manuscript turned out to be a work of a criminal mastermind (who reminded me of a cross between Lord Voldemort and Dr. Evil from Austin Powers movies) who will stop at nothing to show the world how evil he is. I will give a hint: when it comes to being evil, he makes Darth Vader look like a daycare thug. Thursday soon learns that "Lost in a good book" is more than just a nice saying:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424973651i/13825809._SX540_.png" alt="Lost in a Good Book" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only reason I rated this book with 3 stars instead of 2 is the discussion with my buddy readers which turned out to be great fun. There were some amusing parts and references with I would miss had I read this book by my lonely self. <br><br>As I mentioned there were enough amusing moments in the book to qualify it as belonging to humor genre. Unfortunately it was not my type of humor. I always found myself unable to laugh at the situations where innocent bystanders are getting killed in amusing ways by the villains while the noble heroes are protected by the plot armor. It is all fun and games unless you happened to be that bystander. <br><br>I found the character of Thursday Next to be quite shallow. I learned that she suffers from PSD: she is a veteran of Crimea War - in the book England is still at war with Russia over Crimea which took place between 1853 and 1856 in reality. Ask me to name something else about Thursday and I will be at complete loss. <br><br>I mentioned amusing moments. They are unfortunately not too noticeable between author's self-admiration of how clever his writing is and countless uses of deux ex machina. The latter was used so freely and often that I could not see the point of the novel until the second half of it. <br><br>I do admit that some of the complaints I made are related to the fact that this is not my kind of book and I understand people who gave it 5 stars. I also admit that I have not read Jane Eyre (please don't hurt me!) and this fact also diminished my enjoyment of it. At least it made me read the plot summary of the classic I mentioned. This is a good thing, right? Right?<br><br>In the conclusion I would like to thank my buddy readers who made the read much more pleasant experience. Thank you!!! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4724788709523406184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117411302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10152878660877056611"><b>Comment from April 2020</b><br/>I feel bad about this old review. I have now enjoyed a Fforde short story, <b>The Locked Room Mystery</b>, which I gave 4* and reviewed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3271438322' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a>.<br/><br/><b>Review from August 2010</b><br/><br/>I didn't enjoy this. It tries too hard to be clever and to cover many different genres (humour, sci fi, horror, detective, literary and more) whilst also being annoyingly silly. After 100 pages I ditched it - something I rarely do.<br/><br/>Thursday Next is a woman who is a literary detective in one of several alternative realit</span>
  <span id="freeText10152878660877056611" style="display:none"><b>Comment from April 2020</b><br />I feel bad about this old review. I have now enjoyed a Fforde short story, <b>The Locked Room Mystery</b>, which I gave 4* and reviewed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3271438322" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.<br /><br /><b>Review from August 2010</b><br /><br />I didn't enjoy this. It tries too hard to be clever and to cover many different genres (humour, sci fi, horror, detective, literary and more) whilst also being annoyingly silly. After 100 pages I ditched it - something I rarely do.<br /><br />Thursday Next is a woman who is a literary detective in one of several alternative realities round about now. In hers, the Crimean War is still going. Somehow, in her society, manuscripts are stolen and guns are involved; she also manages to get into books and meet characters in them, though I was never convinced as to why any of it happened.<br /><br />WHO... WHY...?<br />I don't understand who this book is written for. You need a love and knowledge of classic literature to know what is our reality and what is an alternative (e.g. whether or not Jane Eyre does marry Rochester), but having those characteristics would seem to me to make one unlikely to enjoy this, though as that is clearly not the case, I am in a minority and evidently missing something.<br /><br />It has a surprisingly colloquial narrative style for a self-consciously "literary" book; jarring Americanisms (a "parking lot") for a British book; basic grammatical errors (using "flaunt" instead of "flout"); too much exposition is delivered in clichéd ways (e.g. a police interview); ludicrous names (Jack Schitt, Acheron Hades (a baddie), Thursday Next, Victor Analogy, a vampire called Stoker, Edmund Capillary and Landen Park-Laine) and even sillier futuristic inventions (pizza by fax and a 2B pencil with built in spell check). <br /><br /><br />Anthony Trollope had a penchant for jokey names, but at least he restricted them to minor characters and made up for it in other ways. This book doesn't.</span>

<div id="review_8110233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8110233" />
    <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan"><img alt="Lisa Vegan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1243394822p2/83445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8110233?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Vegan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Vegan" href="/user/show/83445-lisa-vegan">Lisa Vegan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780670030644" href="/book/show/77020.The_Eyre_Affair">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who enjoy the following: humor, mysteries, sci-fi, fantasy, literature &amp; language</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=1-also-at-librarything">1-also-at-librarything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=readbooks-male-author-or-illust">readbooks-male-author-or-illust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=novel">novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=groups-buddies">groups-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8110233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2589019166316530358">This is a thoroughly delightful and brilliant book. I chuckled and chortled all the way through this book; it’s hilarious. There are many interesting characters and I am eager to read the rest of this series. I’m not sure that the successive books will also get 5 stars from me: the clever premise might get a tad old; I’ll have to see. This unusual story is a bit difficult to define. It fits multiple genres: sci-fi, mystery, humor, fantasy, and fiction. And the author manages to create an entire </span>
  <span id="freeText2589019166316530358" style="display:none">This is a thoroughly delightful and brilliant book. I chuckled and chortled all the way through this book; it’s hilarious. There are many interesting characters and I am eager to read the rest of this series. I’m not sure that the successive books will also get 5 stars from me: the clever premise might get a tad old; I’ll have to see. This unusual story is a bit difficult to define. It fits multiple genres: sci-fi, mystery, humor, fantasy, and fiction. And the author manages to create an entire alternate world, which is something I often enjoy in books when it’s done well, and it’s done exceedingly well here, and with a lot of whimsy. I am now a Jasper Fforde fan: he really pulled off a unique feat in creating this book/series. I suspect I missed some of the references as I have gaps in my knowledge of England and of literature, but I caught enough of the inside jokes to be entertained. I especially enjoyed the portions of the book that were told with Thursday’s voice. (For some reason I kept feeling as though Sue Grafton’s Kinsey Millhone was in Back to the Future. Anyway, it was all a great deal of fun.)<br /><br />Although I loved the book, I suspect that this book is not for everybody. My guess is that a reader would have had to enjoy at least one book from each of the genres listed above to enjoy reading it as much as I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2589019166316530358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137286211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137286211" />
    <a title="Carlos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1037107-carlos"><img alt="Carlos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1274039921p2/1037107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137286211?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carlos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carlos" href="/user/show/1037107-carlos">Carlos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1037107-carlos?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137286211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169408554504878718">Sadly, I found this book to be a major disappointment. I'm huge fan of British comedy and science fiction--Monty Python, Douglas Adams, Dr. Who, Neil Gaiman--and something of an autodidact lit geek, so this novel which promises the exploits of a special agent who has to travel into the novel Jane Eyre in pursuit of a villain sounds right up my alley. So, what went wrong?<br/><br/>Let's start with the world building. While Fforde's alternate universe England is quite inventive, it's also tonally weird. Eng</span>
  <span id="freeText12169408554504878718" style="display:none">Sadly, I found this book to be a major disappointment. I'm huge fan of British comedy and science fiction--Monty Python, Douglas Adams, Dr. Who, Neil Gaiman--and something of an autodidact lit geek, so this novel which promises the exploits of a special agent who has to travel into the novel Jane Eyre in pursuit of a villain sounds right up my alley. So, what went wrong?<br /><br />Let's start with the world building. While Fforde's alternate universe England is quite inventive, it's also tonally weird. England has been locked in the Crimean War all the way into the present day (circa 1985), with no end in sight, and the government appears to be controlled by a large corporation dubbed (unsubtly) the Goliath Corporation. OK, so this is some sort of dystopia, right? But wait, thanks to cloning, scientists have been able to bring dodos out of extinction, and it turns out that they make great pets! Like, OMG!, is that cute or what? The Eyre Affair may be the only dystopic novel I've read in which the Breads and Circuses are intended as much for the reader as for the regime's subjects. (Oh, if only Big Brother had thought to provide everyone with messenger owls, 1984 could have been a much more amusing novel!)<br /><br />Second, there's the use of names. As Roger Ebert once said, "Funny names, in general, are a sign of desperation." I'd like to amend that slightly to say, it's really a bad idea for a novel to feature characters whose names are vastly more interesting than their personalities. Heroine Thursday Next gets a pass, as does main baddy Acheron Hades, but I can't think of anything funny about Paige Turner, Victor Analogy or Alexandria Belfridge.<br /><br />Oh, and let me just say, Acheron Hades' motivation to engage in villainy for no reason because pointless wickedness is the purest form of wickedness? I know it's supposed to make him seem particularly evil, but it just makes him seem arbitrary. I kept expecting the revelation that he was an escapee from a second-rate potboiler.<br /><br />The biggest failure, though, is how panderingly The Eyre Affair wields its metatextuality. Dead British authors are like celebrities in Fforde's England. People change their names to John Milton out of devotion. Robo-Shakespeares quote the bard from every corner. Surrealists somehow manage to spark riots. (This joins with the whole Crimean War aspect to give the sense that England is terribly stagnant. None of the authors that inspire devotion ever saw the 20th century. And surrealism is controversial enough to spark riots? Really, how very quaint.)<br /><br />The scene that really put me off, and which should have inspired me to quit the novel, was the performance of a Rocky Horror version of Richard III, after which a couple of the characters discuss how much they love classic literature. There's something a little jarring about seeing a camped up production of Shakespeare held up as an expression of deep love, as if the Thursday Nextiverse (or even Fforde himself) completely misses the point of camp. Does Fforde think people bring cutlery to midnight showings of The Room because they feel Tommy Wiseau is an auteur?<br /><br />It may be hyperliterate in its use of references, but the effect often feels superficial. In the action revolving around the titular novel, Jane Eyre is reduced to a damsel in distress and Rochester to a straightforward hero, the complex characters I so loved in their original context reduced to cardboard cutouts. Fforde is like a lobotomized Borges, finding ways to dumb down the literature he loves instead of finding new and interesting depths.<br /><br />So, sorry, just did not enjoy this novel. I have to confess though, if I ever got a hold of one of those devices to travel into literature, you know the first thing I'd do? Carpet bomb Fforde's England with copies of every major modernist and postmodernist work from the last century. I'd like to think I'd be treated as a liberator.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12169408554504878718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16637757113872460330">Close the prose portal, the worms are about to start hyphenating!<br/><br/>Hey! Everyone! This is a pretty awesome literature nerd's playground. :)<br/><br/>I kinda expected something like a UF first-person mystery novel with magical elements where characters jump out of the pages of books and make a mess of things, or vice-versa, where we jump in and make a hash of a perfectly good story, but I didn't expect the novel to have a lot of complicated character elements in our main characters, a nicely complicated plot</span>
  <span id="freeText16637757113872460330" style="display:none">Close the prose portal, the worms are about to start hyphenating!<br /><br />Hey! Everyone! This is a pretty awesome literature nerd's playground. :)<br /><br />I kinda expected something like a UF first-person mystery novel with magical elements where characters jump out of the pages of books and make a mess of things, or vice-versa, where we jump in and make a hash of a perfectly good story, but I didn't expect the novel to have a lot of complicated character elements in our main characters, a nicely complicated plot that continues to twist and turn through a LOT more than just the Bronte Society or Jane, herself.<br /><br />And what might be better? Oh, the whole World-Building of the Spec-Ops and the very interesting alternate dimension physics, the whole spy networks associated with missing manuscripts, the Shakespeare Conspiracy, and a (literarily) enormous amount of Lit-Nerd In-Jokes not limited only to conversation, but built right into the world we're thrown into.<br /><br />So is it fantasy, SF (Come on, plasma beams and jumping dimesions lol), a dream of an Editorial Superman or the Wish Fulfilment of every Writer Who Is Also A Fan? Could be it's all of the above. :)<br /><br />This is some really cool fun that reads like a mystery turned into a spy novel, full of magical and SF moments, and a huge focus on characters. What's not to love?</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3989438244444842670">Wow! I just did a quick scan of the reviews for this book and they are all over the place from one to five stars. Some people (like me) love it to death, others really hate it and some just sit in the middle. I guess you have to enjoy Fforde's particular sense of humour.<br/><br/>This was a reread for me but the last time I read it was so long ago the book, when I dug it off my shelf, had turned a yellowy brown colour. This in no way damaged my reading experience. I still loved the premise of the book whi</span>
  <span id="freeText3989438244444842670" style="display:none">Wow! I just did a quick scan of the reviews for this book and they are all over the place from one to five stars. Some people (like me) love it to death, others really hate it and some just sit in the middle. I guess you have to enjoy Fforde's particular sense of humour.<br /><br />This was a reread for me but the last time I read it was so long ago the book, when I dug it off my shelf, had turned a yellowy brown colour. This in no way damaged my reading experience. I still loved the premise of the book which I know is developed into even greater things in the next few books in the series. Thursday Next is a wonderful character and I have a soft spot for Landon and for Pickwick the Dodo.<br /><br />There are many literary references throughout the story which I always enjoy. It has been pointed out that it is a major spoiler for anyone who wants to read Jane Eyre which is funny but also a bit true! <br /><br />Still a five star read for me and now I have read it again I want to carry on and read the rest of them even if they all have yellowy brown pages!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17475988907624284537"><b>Buddy read with the ever amazing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jessica</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6950818.Kristi_Charish' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristi,</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Asya</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31718503-tanya' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tanya</a> and running commentary with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-oosarahoo' rel='nofollow noopener'>oOSarahOo</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29787548-ashley-the-hufflepuff-kitten' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ashley</a> who announced they are stalking our thread <i>(not very good at stalking since we know they are there)</i> over at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/Eyre%20Affair%201_zpsb94acdgm.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/>Think about your favorite book…the one you would live in if you could…the one you would never ever get tired of or want leave. Do you have it firmly in your mind??? Now imagine a world where others love books as much as you and the</span>
  <span id="freeText17475988907624284537" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with the ever amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10336538-jessica-rabid-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Jessica</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7411485-catherine" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6950818.Kristi_Charish" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristi,</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3328287-asya" rel="nofollow noopener">Asya</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/31718503-tanya" rel="nofollow noopener">Tanya</a> and running commentary with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-oosarahoo" rel="nofollow noopener">oOSarahOo</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29787548-ashley-the-hufflepuff-kitten" rel="nofollow noopener">Ashley</a> who announced they are stalking our thread <i>(not very good at stalking since we know they are there)</i> over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a></b><br><br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/Eyre%20Affair%201_zpsb94acdgm.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Think about your favorite book…the one you would live in if you could…the one you would never ever get tired of or want leave. Do you have it firmly in your mind??? Now imagine a world where others love books as much as you and they have found a way to travel inside the pages of said book <b>OR</b> pull characters out.<br><br><b>THIS is a world I would love to go to</b><br><br>THIS is a world made amazing by things like:<br>✘ Cloning kits for extinct species – Thursday has a pet Dodo version 1.2 you know before they started spicing in flamingos and other species.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/efd115b1-ed31-485e-b411-d682fa788c4e_zpsbsn1wfbz.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424733175i/13797252.jpg" alt=" photo efd115b1-ed31-485e-b411-d682fa788c4e_zpsbsn1wfbz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>✘ Bad guys who are somewhat similar to HE-WHO-MUST-NOT-BE-NAMED - <i>He has powers that are slightly baffling. That’s why we can’t say his name. I call it Rule Number One.” “His name? Why not?” <b>“Because he can hear his own name—even whispered—over a thousand-yard radius, perhaps more. He uses it to sense our presence.”</b></i><br><br>✘ Genetically sequenced bookworms that have a semi conscience hive mind and eat prepositions and poop out punctuation, more so when they get excited. <i>"they had just digested a recent meal of prepositions and were happily farting out apostrophes and ampersands; the air was heav'y with th'em&amp;"</i><br><br>✘ An uncle with wonderous and magical inventions in his basement lab including a car with a cameleon paint job.<br><a href="http://s1267.photobucket.com/user/FionaFixit/media/thursdaycar2signed_zps9kfqwvpr.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424733175i/13797253.jpg" alt=" photo thursdaycar2signed_zps9kfqwvpr.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>✘ A world where people don’t talk about what is on the television so much as they debate over who really wrote the works of Shakespeare and there are a good many theories floating around on that one.<br><br>✘ Plays that have cult followings like the Rocky Horror Picture show and the audience participates in the entire production.<br><i>“When is the winter of our discontent?” “Now,” replied Richard with a cruel smile, “is the winter of our discontent . . .”<br>“. . . made glorious summer by this son of York,” continued Richard, limping to the side of the stage. <b>On the word “ summer” six hundred people placed sunglasses on and looked up at an imaginary sun.</b></i><br><br>✘ Thursday also has a father whose face it seems could stop time like literally. - <i>My father had a face that could stop a clock. I don’t mean that he was ugly or anything; it was a phrase the ChronoGuard used to describe someone <b>who had the power to reduce time to an ultraslow trickle.</b></i><br><br><b>This book is for book lovers, like serious book lovers.</b> It has a gazillion little play on words, literary references, and random shout outs to books that it was a fantastic treat for me. It would still be pretty enjoyable if you didn’t know a lot about most of the books mentioned but it is a little more fun if you are in on the hidden gems.<br><br>The plot really didn’t start happening until the second half of the book but I was having such a good time with all the fantastical gadgets, references and happenings that I didn’t really care.<br><br>However I totally enjoyed myself and liked the little bit of romance, chase of the bad guy and trip through the pages of Jane Eyre. I had a great time reading this and much like <i>Hitchhikers Guide to the Galaxy</i> there are a lot of random happenings that end up leading down a path to the plot eventually. It isn’t something I can read everyday but when in the correct mood it is a wonderful adventure.<br><br>This book wraps up nicely so that you could just stop the series here or chose to carry on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17475988907624284537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2880123782706083337">3.5★<br/><br/>This book did sound <b>so</b> up my alley and I'm a bit worried because it is a very <i>busy</i> book , so maybe it wasn't the right book to start in a very active holiday. I'm hoping my rating is fair.<br/><br/>I found it very hard to get into the start -as I said busy. It reminded me of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372299.The_Hitch_Hiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_A_Trilogy_in_Five_Parts' title='The Hitch Hiker's Guide to the Galaxy A Trilogy in Five Parts by Douglas Adams' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Hitch Hiker's Guide to the Galaxy: A Trilogy in Five Parts</a> but the style was much colder - I just couldn't warm to any of the characters at all.   <span id="freeText2880123782706083337" style="display:none">3.5★<br><br>This book did sound <b>so</b> up my alley and I'm a bit worried because it is a very <i>busy</i> book , so maybe it wasn't the right book to start in a very active holiday. I'm hoping my rating is fair.<br><br>I found it very hard to get into the start -as I said busy. It reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372299.The_Hitch_Hiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_A_Trilogy_in_Five_Parts" title="The Hitch Hiker's Guide to the Galaxy A Trilogy in Five Parts by Douglas Adams" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hitch Hiker's Guide to the Galaxy: A Trilogy in Five Parts</a> but the style was much colder - I just couldn't warm to any of the characters at all. That did make it a struggle for me to keep going with the read.<br><br><i>However,</i> Every time I would consider giving up there would be another witticism <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I was in '78 recently," he announced. "I brought you this."<br>He handed me a single by the Beatles. I didn't recognize the title.<br>"Didn't they split in '70?"<br>"Not always. How are things?”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>or some lines that were laugh out loud funny;<br><blockquote>
  <i>"Can't we wait for the Chronoguard?"<br>"They'd never get here in time. It's easy. A lobotomised monkey could do it."<br>"And where are we going to get a lobotomised monkey at this time of night"</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The wild and uncertain tone of the book improved for me at around 64% - although I didn't really like the ending.<br><br>So it was a real mixed bag and I may have to read another Fforde to decide if I like his style or not.<br><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_14379669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14379669" />
    <a title="Krista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/638605-krista"><img alt="Krista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205023095p2/638605.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14379669?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krista" href="/user/show/638605-krista">Krista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/638605-krista?shelf=read-in-2007">read-in-2007</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14379669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8713426447176497479">(Violence alert: The body count is high, plus some grossness factor.)<br/>It’s a spy thriller. No, wait — it’s science fiction. No, wait — it’s literary criticism. No, wait — it’s art history. No, wait — it’s historical-political commentary. No, wait — it’s romantic comedy. No, wait — it’s an epic war drama. No, wait — it’s — oh, look — Japanese tourists!<br/><br/>While I applaud the spirit of many of the directions this novel takes, you kind of have to wonder if the author could have focused just a tad bit mo</span>
  <span id="freeText8713426447176497479" style="display:none">(Violence alert: The body count is high, plus some grossness factor.)<br />It’s a spy thriller. No, wait — it’s science fiction. No, wait — it’s literary criticism. No, wait — it’s art history. No, wait — it’s historical-political commentary. No, wait — it’s romantic comedy. No, wait — it’s an epic war drama. No, wait — it’s — oh, look — Japanese tourists!<br /><br />While I applaud the spirit of many of the directions this novel takes, you kind of have to wonder if the author could have focused just a tad bit more...<br /><br />So here’s the interesting aspect of this novel: Fforde envisions an alternate reality in which wars are (literally) waged over ideas, a fantasy in which literature and art are at the center of people’s daily concerns. In one incidental moment, the main character turns on the TV in her hotel room; a news reporter is reporting on riots that broke out while Neoclassicists were protesting the 10-year anniversary of the legalization of Surrealism. <br /><br />Eventually (three-quarters of the way through the novel), the main event occurs: an English professor gone bad kidnaps Jane Eyre from page 100-something of the original manuscript, erasing the text of the remaining pages from all copies of the book and causing millions of Jane Eyre fans to come out of the woodwork and hold weepy candlelight vigils.<br /><br />Our heroine, LiteraTec (literary detective) Thursday Next, must restore Jane to her rightful place in the novel, keep the evil villian away from Miss Eyre, and supervise the plot from inside the book as the book "rewrites" itself. Things go awry, of course, and the original manuscript is compromised — but with felicitous consequences for Miss Eyre, Mr. Rochester, and Jane Eyre fans everywhere.<br /><br />Of course, the author of a book like this must hope to capitalize on a pre-existing Jane Eyre fan base...but the danger in writing derivative literary fiction is that, while your book may be a perfectly good book in many ways, you are putting your reader in mind of really great literature, next to which your book is doomed to lose by comparison. And as the plot of Jane Eyre droned on from Thursday Next's perspective, I couldn’t help thinking, "I’d rather be reading Jane Eyre."<br /><br />The final twist in the love story is, I have to admit, cute — but not cute enough for me to recommend the book, at least not to someone exactly like me. However, if a heavy dose of violence doesn’t make you queasy and you can hold on for a roller-coaster ride of genre-bending twists and turns, you might enjoy the cleverness of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8713426447176497479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
